               UNIVERSITY CITY CENTER TRAFFIC IMPACT ANALYSIS

                                     EXCECUTIVE SUMMARY

This document presents the results of the traffic impact analysis prepared for a multi-use
development, University City Center, proposed by CIBMM, LLC, on the site of the existing Holiday
Inn at the intersection of Prices Fork Road and University City Boulevard in Blacksburg, VA. This
analysis analyzes the proposed development in two parts. Study A analyzes the demolition of the
existing 16,049 square foot (SF) restaurant and bar and replacing it with new off-campus student
housing units containing 495 beds while retaining the existing 137 room motel. Study B analyzes
the demolition of the existing 16,049 SF bar and restaurant and replacing it with new off-campus
student housing units containing 495 beds and demolishing the existing 137 room motel and
replacing it with 15,000 SF of retail and 260 motel rooms. Additionally, a no-build analysis is also
provided.

For this study, traffic volumes are derived for site build out year 2015 and for year 2022 from 2013
data. The derivation assumes a 0.5% annual growth rate. Development scheduled for the adjacent
Virginia Tech campus will change current traffic flow characteristics over the next decade. Traffic
data for the street network surrounding this study's site have been previously analyzed for the
Virginia Tech development plan in Precinct B by Whitman, Requardt, and Associates (WR&A) and
the network analysis Synchro software traffic models are utilized at approach intersections to the
University City Center site.

This analysis addresses the traffic impacts of the proposed development on the surrounding
transportation network. Based on direction from the Town of Blacksburg, the study area includes
the following intersections:

        Prices Fork Road (Route 412) and University City Boulevard
        Prices Fork Road (Route 412) and West Campus Drive/Woodland Drive
        University City Boulevard and Kroger Fuel Entrance/University Mall Entrance
        University City Boulevard and Glade Road
        Two entrances to the site:
                One new from Prices Fork Road
                One existing from University City Boulevard


This study has approached the analysis of the proposed development in a conservative manner
utilizing the full trip generation rates for apartments for the student housing. It is highly likely that
the land use will not produce this number of trips for several reasons:




                                                    i                  K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
   1. Many students will not have classes at times requiring travel during the roadway traffic peak
       hours.
   2. Some students may choose to walk or ride bicycles to campus for housing this close to
       campus.
   3. Some students may choose to ride the bus, which has routes in the immediate vicinity.


The analysis for the proposed site development indicates that the signalized intersections of the
existing street network has certain traffic movements that currently exhibit less than desirable
operations (levels of service and delays). The analyses in this study indicate that the proposed
development will not exacerbate the operations of these critical movements, particularly at the
signalized intersection most affected by the development, the intersection of Prices Fork Road and
University City Boulevard. Existing problem operations at the West Campus Drive intersection are
for traffic entering and exiting the Virginia Tech campus. Due to the relatively small volume of
traffic generated by the proposed site, the development has virtually no effect on this intersection.
Likewise, the effect on the intersections of University City Boulevard with the Kroger Fuel Station
and Glade Road intersections are minimal with no reduction in levels of service.


Based on the analysis and the desire for efficient traffic operations, the following recommendations
are offered:


Recommendations:
       Based on the analysis performed in this study, the following recommendations are made:


       1.       Eliminate the two existing entrances to the site on Prices Fork Road. Construct a new
            right in/right out only entrance from Prices Fork Road which lines up with the proposed
            parking garage entrance. Provide minimum 100 foot long right turn lane for entrance.
       2.       Construct continuous westbound right turn from new right turn lane past new
            entrance to tie into existing westbound right turn lane at the signalized intersection of
            Prices Fork Road and University City Boulevard.
       3.       Close existing median crossover on Prices Fork Road. Construct a new median


                                                  ii                K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
     crossover with a restricted left in that aligns with new site entrance. Utilize separator
     design crossover, if space allows. Provide one-way sign on median opposite new
     entrance facing west.
4.      Add overlap phase on the signal at the intersection of Prices Fork Road and
     University City Boulevard such that the westbound right movement is protected
     simultaneously with the southbound split phase.

I.   INTRODUCTION


     A. Purpose


          University City Center is a multi-use development proposed by CIBMM, LLC in
          Blacksburg, Virginia. The site is located in the northeast corner of the intersection of
          Prices Fork Road (Route 412) and University City Boulevard.               The existing site
          contains a 137 room Holiday Inn motel and 16,049 square foot (SF) restaurant with
          bar and grill. Figure 1 shows an aerial photo of the site.


          The existing site consists of a 137 room motel and a 16,049 square foot (SF) bar and
          restaurant.


          The impacts to traffic on the adjacent streets of the proposed development will be
          analyzed in two parts, designated Study A (partial-redevelopment) and Study B (full
          redevelopment). Study A analyzes the development proposed with the initial PRD
          submittal. Study A analyzes the demolition of the existing 16,049 SF restaurant and
          construction of new off-campus student housing, containing 495 beds and retains the
          existing 137 room motel. Study B anticipates complete redevelopment of the entire
          site and analyzes the demolition of the existing 16,049 SF restaurant and the existing
          137 room motel and constructs the same new off-campus student housing containing
          495 beds. It is currently anticipated that upon demolition of the existing motel, the
          proposed development will also include 15,000 SF of retail and 260 motel rooms.
          Both development scenarios include a 692 space parking structure.


          This study analyzes existing (year 2013) traffic on the adjacent streets and the
          impacts to traffic in two future years, 2015 and 2022. Year 2015 is the anticipated
          future build out year for the proposed redevelopment of the University City Center



                                             1                  K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
Figure 1
site. The Year 2022 corresponds to the anticipated full build out of the proposed
development of the facilities in Virginia Tech's Precinct B area.


The consulting firm of Whitman, Requardt and Associates (WR&A) has performed a
traffic study for the proposed developments at Virginia Tech's Precinct B area for the
Town of Blacksburg. Precinct B is on the north side of campus bounded by West
Campus Drive and Prices Fork Road and in the vicinity of the University City Center
site. The redevelopment will affect traffic movements along Prices Fork Road and
completion of construction at Precinct B is anticipated by 2022. The Town requested
that this study consider the impacts of the Precinct B construction to better reflect the
ultimate impacts to the Prices Fork Road and University City Boulevard street
network. The Synchro traffic analyses computer software models developed for the
Virginia Tech Precinct B study have been used to develop the street network for this
study.


Proposed access to the site is from two locations for both Study A and Study B:
         Location A is from Prices Fork Road approximately 400 feet from the
         intersection of Prices Fork Road and University City Boulevard. A relocated
         median crossover with a restricted left in only from Prices Fork Road with a
         130 foot long left turn lane. A right in/right out only entrance at the median
         crossover will be constructed for ingress and egress to the site. A 100 foot
         long right turn lane will be provided for westbound traffic. This right turn
         lane will be constructed continuous from the proposed entrance to the
         signalized intersection at University City Boulevard. Left turns from the site
         onto Prices Fork Road will not be allowed. The two existing entrances to the
         existing Holiday Inn site and the existing crossover will be removed with the
         construction of the new entrance.
         Location B is from University City Boulevard via the existing intersection of
         University City Boulevard and the New River Valley Community Services




                                   2                  K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
             parking area/University City Mall parking entrances. This is an unsignalized,
             full service intersection.


      This report summarizes the findings of the Traffic Impact Analysis (TIA) associated
      with the potential impacts to the adjacent street network resulting from traffic
      generated by the proposed use of the property.


B. Site Location and Study Area


      The site is located at the intersection of Prices Fork Road and University City
      Boulevard in the northeast corner. See Figure 2 for an aerial view of the site.


      At the Town of Blacksburg's request, the study area consists of the following
      intersections:


             Prices Fork Road (Route 412) and University City Boulevard
             Prices Fork Road (Route 412) and West Campus Drive/Woodland Drive
             University City Boulevard and Kroger Fuel Entrance/University Mall
             Entrance
             University City Boulevard and Glade Road
             Two entrances to the site:
            One from Prices Fork Road (Location A)
            One from University City Boulevard (Location B)


C. Existing Land Use and Surrounding Area


      The existing site is a 137 room Holiday Inn and 16,049 SF restaurant with bar and
      grill. The surrounding area is a combination of retail, commercial development, and
      the Virginia Tech campus community. University City Boulevard serves as the major
      route for vehicles accessing the commercial and retail establishments around the


                                          3              K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
Figure 2
            University Mall complex. Prices Fork Road provides access to the Virginia Tech
            campus parking facilities as well as serving as a thoroughfare for traffic from U.S.
            Route 460, a limited access highway, to Main Street in the Town of Blacksburg.


      D. Proposed Land Use


            Study A proposes the demolition of the existing restaurant and bar and the
            construction of off-campus student housing units with 495 beds. Study A leaves the
            existing 137 room motel in place.


            Study B proposes the demolition of the existing site and the construction of a total of
            off-campus student housing units with 495 beds, 15,000 SF of retail space, 260 motel
            rooms are proposed by the developer.


            Figure 3 and Figure 4 depict the proposed Study A and Study B development site
            plans, respectively.


II.   ANALYSIS OF EXISTING (2013) CONDITIONS


      A. Peak Hour Traffic Volumes

                   West Campus Drive and Prices Fork Road; February 14, 2013 and April 10,
                   2012.
                   University City Boulevard and Prices Fork Road; February 14, 2013.
                   University City Boulevard and Kroger Fuel Entrance; April 24, 2013.
                   University City Boulevard and Glade Road; April 11, 2013




                                              4                  K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
Figure 3
Figure 4
      It is assumed that each of these counts was taken under typical weekday traffic. The
      counts indicate that weekday peak hour traffic occurs between 8:30 and 9:30 in the
      morning, and between 4:45 and 5:45 in the evening. These counts have been
      balanced for existing condition analysis by WR&A for use in the Virginia Tech
      Precinct B report. The balanced model is used in this report for existing conditions.
      The turning movement summary counts are contained in Appendix A. Figure 5
      presents the results of the balanced AM and PM peak hour turning movement counts
      at each intersection.


B. Existing Levels of Service


      Traffic operations at an intersection are measured in terms of "Level of Service'
      (LOS). Level of service is a quantitative measure of driver perception of delay
      (waiting time) experienced at an intersection, and LOS is based on the delay
      thresholds specified in the 2010 Highway Capacity Manual (HCM). LOS conditions
      range from "A" (little delay) to "F" (very long delay). Table 1 reflects the delay
      ranges in seconds drivers may experience for a corresponding level of service for
      both signalized and unsignalized intersections. The criteria used to measure LOS for
      signalized intersections is different from the criteria used for unsignalized
      intersections. LOS for signalized intersections is based on control delay per vehicle.
      Control delay, as defined by HCM, includes initial deceleration delay, queue move-
      up time, stopped delay and final acceleration delay. According to this definition the
      minimum design acceptable delay is "D" for design purposes, particularly in a more
      developed area. However, LOS E may be acceptable for existing signal installations.
       For signalized intersections, Level of Service F indicates that more than one signal
      change cycle may be required for a driver to pass through the intersection. For
      unsignalized intersections, levels of service are based on critical gap, the minimum
      time interval in the major street traffic stream that allows entry for one minor street
      vehicle from an intersection, particularly the left turn vehicles. Level of service "E"
      is generally considered to be the minimum design standard. At an unsignalized
      intersection, LOS F occurs when there are not enough minimum gaps to allow the


                                        5                  K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
movements on the minor street to enter the major street in a "reasonable" amount of
time.




                                 6                 K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
                                      TABLE 1
                      LEVELS OF SERVICE AND DELAY
   UNSIGNALIZED INTERSECTION                   SIGNALIZED INTERSECTION
                       Average Control                               Average Control
                      Delay Per Vehicle                              Delay Per Vehicle
   Level of Service       (Seconds)           Level of Service            (Seconds)

          A                  0-10                    A                        0-10
          B                  10-15                   B                       10-20
          C                  15-25                   C                       20-35
          D                  25-35                   D                       35-55
          E                  35-50                   E                       55-80
          F                  >50                     F                        >80


       Synchro traffic software was used to analyze all signalized intersections in this
       report. SimTraffic simulation software was used in conjunction with Synchro to
       further analyze vehicle queuing results. The procedures used by Synchro and
       SimTraffic are in accordance with the methodologies stated in the Highway Capacity
       Manual 2010 (HCM) for intersection analysis.


       Analysis results for signalized intersections provide level of service calculations for
       all approaches as well as an overall intersection level of service. Please note that
       analysis results for unsignalized intersections do not provide level of service results
       for all approaches or an overall intersection level of service, but rather a level of
       service for movements and/or approaches that have a conflicting movement. In this
       study, level of service is the basis for the evaluation of existing and background
       traffic conditions and the impacts of the traffic generated by the proposed site on the
       existing roadway network

             Virginia Tech Precinct B study. The intersection of University City Boulevard and
             Prices Fork Road experiences LOS F for the westbound right turn during the PM
             peak hour due to the through movement queue blocking the right turn lane.

III.   ANALYSIS OF FUTURE CONDITIONS WITHOUT DEVELOPMENT


       A. Peak Hour Traffic Volumes


             The existing, balanced 2013 traffic counts were converted to 2015 data by assuming
             an annual growth rate of 0.5% from year 2013. The counts at the intersection of
             University City Boulevard and Glade Road and at the intersection of University City
             Boulevard and the Kroger Fuel/University Mall Entrances were converted to 2022
             data by assuming an annual growth rate of 0.5% from year 2013. Data for year 2022
             at the intersection of University City Boulevard and Prices Fork Road and at the
             intersection of Prices Fork Road and West Campus Drive were provided by the
             WR&A Virginia Tech Precinct B Traffic Study. The 2013 turning movement
             summary counts are contained in Appendix A.



                                              10                  K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
B. Existing Site Trip Generation


       The existing Holiday Inn site generates vehicle trips currently that are included in the
       existing traffic counts made for this study and the Virginia Tech Precinct B study.
       To evaluate conditions at the existing entrances, trips from the existing land uses on
       the site were generated using typical ITE land use codes and distributed based upon
       observations and local knowledge. The total existing trips from the site are indicated
       in Table 5. Trips generated to and from the site for the AM and PM peak hours for
       the 2015 No-Build and 2022 No-Build scenarios are depicted in Figures 6-A, 6-B, 7-
       A, and 7-B. The trips shown in these figures are accounted for in the intersection
       counts in Appendix A and therefore these trips are absorbed into the network at the
       following intersection from which they were generated. Figures 6-A through 7-B
       indicate the trips generated for the existing site. Further discussion on trip generation
       for the proposed site development is provided in Sections IV and V.

As expected for the short, three year period of traffic growth, the analyses indicate
that all approaches for the intersection of University City Boulevard and Kroger
Fuels Entrance and the intersection of University City Boulevard and Glade Road
experience acceptable levels of service under 2015 No-Build conditions. The
intersection of Prices Fork Road and West Campus Drive and the intersection of
University City Boulevard and Prices Fork Road experience substandard levels of
service. The intersection of Prices Fork Road and West Campus Drive experiences
LOS F for the eastbound right and the northbound left during the AM peak hour and
a LOS F in the PM peak hour for the northbound right. This condition is addressed in
the Virginia Tech Precinct B study. The intersection of University City Boulevard
and Prices Fork Road experiences LOS E for the westbound right due to the through
movement queue blocking the right turn lane. The southbound right experiences LOS
F during the PM peak hour.


The unsignalized intersections modeled for the 2015 No-Build condition show poor
levels of service for the westbound left and through movement for the intersection of
University City Boulevard and Site Entrance Location #3 and at the southbound left
and right movement for the intersection of Prices Fork Road and Site Entrance
Location #3 in the PM peak hour. Both of these locations are the exiting movements
from the site.


Note: The traffic volume projections for 2015 are derived from the 2013 traffic
counts with an annual growth percentage of 0.5% for the three year period.

IV.   TRIP GENERATION


      Site generated traffic was estimated using the methodology from the ITE Trip Generation
      Manual, 7th Edition. Based upon the type of development proposed, the appropriate land use
      code must be selected from the ITE Manual to generate the corresponding trips. For this
      study's proposed development of a mixed-use site the following land use (LU) codes were
      utilized:



                                              18                 K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
         220 ­ Apartment
         320 ­ Motel
         881 ­ Pharmacy/Drugstore with Drive-Through Window
         931 ­ Quality Restaurant


The Apartment land use was used for the proposed student-housing units with 495 beds.
Although there may be only 100-150 student apartments proposed, considering that college
students exhibit atypical trip behaviors, this study considers each bedroom in the
development as a separate dwelling unit. The average rate of vehicular trips generated per
dwelling unit is 0.51 in the AM peak hour and 0.62 in the PM peak hour. These trip
generation rates appear conservative as many students would not have classes starting at or
before 9:00 AM and not ending as late as 5:00 PM. Furthermore, the utilization of the
Apartment land use code to represent college students does not accounts for a college
student's potential usage of alternate modes of transportation (bicycle, mass transit, walking,
etc.).


Land Use 320 was used for the existing motel and the proposed motel trip generation.


Land Use 881 was used for the 15,000 SF of retail space trip generation.


Land Use 931 was used for the existing bar and restaurant trip generation.


Total trip generations were calculated for each of the three scenarios: No-build, Study A and
Study B. The trips were generated by considering the scenario's proposed development and
independently tabulating the trips generated per the individual land use. The individual land
use trips were then reasonably distributed by the percentage entering and exiting the site at
each entrance. The trips for the land uses being demolished were subtracted from the total
proposed trips. Finally, the total, entering and exiting values were summed to provide the
development's total net trips entering and exiting the site. Table 5 presents the trips
generated by the proposed development scenarios.


                                          19                 K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
V.   TRIP DISTRIBUTION


     The distribution of trips onto the existing street network was evaluated based on discussions
     with the Town of Blacksburg and the site's developer. The No-Build scenario distributes
     trips across the existing three entrances in an even distribution for both entering and exiting
     movements. Study A and Study B assume that 65% of trips will enter the site from Prices
     Fork Road and that 60% will exit the site via University City Boulevard. For all scenarios,
     the University City Boulevard site entrance is shared by the adjacent parking area for New
     River Valley Community Services (NRVCS). The NRVCS parking area contains 177
     parking spaces. For this study, it was assumed that 130 vehicles would enter the parking area
     in the AM and that 130 vehicles would exit in the PM. The study assumed that 110 vehicles
     would enter from the south and 20 from the north in the AM, and that 110 would exit to the
     south and 20 to the north in the PM.


     This study conservatively analyzes the potential impacts by the proposed development to the
     existing road network by assuming that all trips generated will be traveled by vehicle.


     A. No-Build


            The existing site will yield 72 trips in the AM and 188 trips in the PM peak hours.
            For this study, these trips are distributed evenly across the three existing site
            entrances


     B. Study A


            The Study A site will yield 293 trips in the AM and 238 in the PM peak hours. 65%
            of the entering trips will enter the site from the Prices Fork Road entrance. 60% of
            the exiting trips will exit the site from University City Boulevard.




                                               20                 K:\Projects\33\3344\TIA Report\3344-TIA.doc
        It is anticipated that 65% of the site traffic will enter the site from Prices Fork Road
        to access the parking garage immediately within the development. Furthermore, the
        majority of traffic adjacent to the site will be coming from either US Route 460 to
        the west or the Virginia Tech campus from the east.


        It is anticipated that 60% of the site traffic will exit onto University City Boulevard.
        Students leaving the site will predominately travel to the Virginia Tech campus.
        This is the more efficient egress point due to the restricted left-in and right-in/right-
        out only entrance on Prices Fork Road. Furthermore, frequent motel guests will
        utilize the University City Boulevard entrance as a learned movement to access
        major events at Virginia Tech and/or the Town of Blacksburg. The majority of
        traffic using this exit is anticipated to travel south on University City Boulevard.


C. Study B


        The Study B will yield 320 trips in the AM and 526 in the peak hours. Trip
        distribution and rational for Study B is equivalent to that of Study A.

in this study.

                                 36
VIII.   QUEUEING ANALYSIS


        Queue lengths for the AM and PM peak hour periods were analyzed for all scenarios at
        specific intersection and locations as follows. Queue lengths were analyzed by SimTraffic
        with a multiple run analysis. SimTraffic queue reports are included in Appendix D. Tables
        2, 3, 4, 6, 7, 8, and 9 present the queuing results for critical intersections in this study.


        Queue at the westbound approach through lanes at the intersection of University City
        Boulevard and Prices Fork Road is less than the proposed right turn lane extension storage
        length in all peak hours for both Study A and Study B.


 IX.    CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS


        A.      Conclusions


        The existing study area contains levels of service below optimal, specifically at the
        intersection of University City Boulevard and Prices Fork Road and the intersection of
        Prices Fork Road and West Campus Drive. Levels of service at these intersections are at or
        below Level E for the AM and PM peak hours. As seen in the 2022 traffic volumes derived
        by WR&A's study and corresponding LOS tables (Tables 4, 7 and 9), the planned
        development in Precinct B will begin to divert some of the future traffic volume away from
        the Prices Fork corridor and improve the street network.


        As indicated in Table 5 a total of 531 trips will be generated by the Study A development
        and 846 trips will be generated by Study B.




        B.      Recommendations


        Based on the analysis performed in this study, the following recommendations are made:


                                                   37
     5.      Eliminate the two existing entrances to the site on Prices Fork Road. Construct a new
          right in/right out only entrance from Prices Fork Road which lines up with the proposed
          parking garage entrance. Provide minimum 100 foot long right turn lane for entrance.
     6.      Construct continuous westbound right turn from new right turn lane past new
          entrance to tie into existing westbound right turn lane at the signalized intersection of
          Prices Fork Road and University City Boulevard.
     7.      Close existing median crossover on Prices Fork Road. Construct a new median
          crossover to align with new site entrance. Utilize separator design crossover, if space
          allows. Provide one-way sign on median opposite new entrance facing west.
     8.      Add overlap phase on the signal at the intersection of Prices Fork Road and
          University City Boulevard such that the westbound right movement is protected
          simultaneously with the southbound split phase.
